## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, characteristic of chemical rate laws. The rate likely follows mass-action kinetics where dA/dt depends on powers of A, possibly with time-dependent modulation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface catalysis with adsorption)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Parallel pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous reaction channels)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power dependence on concentration → elementary reaction with molecularity equal to the power (mass action law)
- Linear dependence on A (dA/dt ∝ A) → first-order kinetics leading to exponential decay A(t) = A0*exp(-kt)
- Quadratic dependence on A (dA/dt ∝ A²) → second-order kinetics leading to reciprocal time dependence 1/A ∝ t
- Rational function of A with saturation → enzyme or surface-catalyzed reaction with limited active sites
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth where product catalyzes its own formation
- Constant additive term independent of A → zero-order source/sink term indicating constant production or external feed
- Explicit time dependence in rate law → non-isothermal conditions, photochemical initiation, or external forcing
- Negative sign convention → consumption of reactant (dA/dt < 0 when A > 0 indicates A is being consumed)
- Sum of power-law terms with different exponents → competing parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Denominator polynomial in A → adsorption or complexation effects reducing effective reaction rate at high concentrations
